","id":"260aa4b0-3257-11ef-b424-5d0c30e34775","slug":"content-management--1107218241672","wordpressId":null,"postTagJoin":{"PostId":"611cc7b0-1291-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"260aa4b0-3257-11ef-b424-5d0c30e34775"}},{"name":"OPEN SOURCE","id":"1188f5c4-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"open-source","wordpressId":"22","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"611cc7b0-1291-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"1188f5c4-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}},{"name":"Umbraco","id":"130b5006-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"umbraco","wordpressId":"56","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"611cc7b0-1291-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"130b5006-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}},{"name":"Websites","id":"e4e33170-e236-11ee-a2a9-e16a7317f091","slug":"websites","wordpressId":null,"postTagJoin":{"PostId":"611cc7b0-1291-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"e4e33170-e236-11ee-a2a9-e16a7317f091"}}],"postProduct":{"id":"5ea5a5d0-1294-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","postId":"611cc7b0-1291-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","productId":"3b275ce0-f8c3-11ed-843f-05f7aa84865d"},"campaignPost":null,"minutesToRead":9},{"name":"Accessibility Needs Heroes, and Lucy Greco Brings a Paralympian’s Heart to the Digital Field","intro":"In my conversation with the digital equality speaker and web accessibility evangelist, we leaned into the challenges of institutional culture change, the emerging concerns around AI, and her restless commitment to creating a more inclusive world.","content":"\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen I started my call with \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/lucy-greco-968b491/\"\u003eLucy Greco,\u003c/a\u003e there was an unmistakable bark in the background.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA pooch? Could be. They’re common fixtures during Zoom calls in the gig economy. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs it happens, Lucy is blind. So I assumed it might be her guide dog, whom I had become acquainted with at our \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/a-gathering-of-content-champions-heres-why-cms-connect-25-was-super-in-every-way\"\u003eBoye \u0026amp; Company CMS Connect\u003c/a\u003e event in Montreal last August. That’s where I first saw her speak on the critical topic of digital accessibility.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eGuide dogs are a breed apart, capable of navigating the world with uncanny sensitivity and intuition. It takes about \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.guidingeyes.org/guide-dogs-101/\"\u003etwo years to fully train one,\u003c/a\u003e and each handler, like Lucy, is matched based on specific criteria like pace and lifestyle. Along the way, they form a deep physical and emotional bond that centers on trust.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut no, the puppy in question was one of two she was currently fostering – with two more arriving the following day. Her upper threshold, I learned, is \u003ci\u003eseven\u003c/i\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I thought the new puppy was sleeping, but she was trying to chew the cables under my desk,\" she cajoled. “We’ve got a full house.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat’s Lucy for you. Right at home with pushing the upper limits, doing it all with unapologetic joy, blunt honesty, and a heart as wide as an Albertan prairie. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo call her a champion would be putting it mildly. Growing up in Calgary, she told me about her exploits as a \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://paralympic.ca/\"\u003eCanadian Paralympian,\u003c/a\u003e competing in the sport of \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.paralympic.org/goalball/about\"\u003eGoalball\u003c/a\u003e. Invented in 1946 to help rehabilitate veterans who had lost their sight during the Second World War, it’s a fast-paced team sport designed for blind and visually impaired athletes. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHere’s the fascinating part: Goalball is played in silence. It has to be. This allows players to hear the sport’s weighted ball, which is imbued with bells. Participants use auditory tracking and tactile floor markings to defend their goal and score against opponents. It requires agility, speed, and team communication – and at the Paralympics level, an athleticism that is off the charts.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"media\"\u003e\u003cdiv data-oembed-url=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MuUuB_FN7Bg\"\u003e\u003cdiv style=\"position:relative;padding-bottom:100%;height:0;padding-bottom:56.2493%\"\u003e\u003ciframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/MuUuB_FN7Bg\" style=\"position:absolute;width:100%;height:100%;top:0;left:0\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; encrypted-media\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It's specifically made for blind people,” Lucy explained. “You can describe it as a combination of soccer, bowling, and Chinese handball. Or, the way I prefer to describe it is, ‘You play dodgeball to lose.’”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ci\u003eDodgeball to lose\u003c/i\u003e. But everything about it \u003ci\u003efeels\u003c/i\u003e like winning.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eMaybe it’s her tenacious spirit that has driven Lucy to the top of her game, both personally and professionally. As a life-long web accessibility evangelist, she's focused her superpowers on technology as an activator for inclusive digital experiences. But finding success was a crucible – one that required perseverance.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“As an athlete, I really wanted to grow up to be a physical therapist,” she reminisced. “Going to school in the 80s and 90s as a blind person, things like anatomy and biology, which were key to physical therapy, were not accessible to me. It was just completely out.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat barrier shaped everything that followed, and for the last 25 years, she’s worked tirelessly to break down walls and create opportunities. She’s done that principally through her work at \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://accessaces.com/\"\u003eAccess Aces,\u003c/a\u003e a consulting firm that provides training, policy guidance, W3C evaluations, UI/UX best practices, and strategic planning services for a wide range of institutions. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs her website proclaims, \u003ci\u003e“Lucy makes accessibility easy!”\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAchieving that promise? Not so easy. It requires her to always remain at the cutting edge with assistive technologies – something she did in spades during her tenure at the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.berkeley.edu/\"\u003eUniversity of California at Berkeley.\u003c/a\u003e In her role as an evangelist, she leveraged her expertise to transform the accessibility posture across the University’s campus, helping to lead the school to a more inclusive future. This included evaluations, system-wide testing, tool procurement, and more.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAlong the way, Lucy became a passionate firebrand, a fierce warrior who uses her voice to ignite change. She speaks regularly – and passionately – on a range of accessibility topics. Over the course of her career, she’s supported countless people with physical and motor impairments, helping them to successfully master a spectrum of tools that augment communication and input. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:86.79%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/lucy-greco-presenting-boye-cms-connect-2026.png\" alt=\"\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eLucy Greco presenting at the CMS Connect Conference in 2025. Source: Janus Boye/Seb Barre archive\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDuring my own stints as a digital practitioner, accessibility has been a central topic – and a persistently elusive one. I’ve personally managed numerous remediation projects, working extensively with platforms like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/siteimproveai-redefines-accessibility-and-performance-with-unified-agentic-content-intelligence-platform\"\u003eSiteimprove\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/acquia-to-acquire-monsido-expands-partnerships-to-offer-complete-digital-experience-optimization\"\u003eMonsido\u003c/a\u003e. Despite having more tools at our disposal, accessibility is still treated as an afterthought. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAfter hearing an inspiring talk from \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/habengirma/\"\u003eHaben Girma\u003c/a\u003e – the first deafblind graduate of Harvard Law School – I realized just how wide this gap is. As such, I’ve written frequently about developing academic and industry resources on accessible design philosophy and the ethics of inclusion.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut the problem is so big that it requires all of us to solve it. Last year’s \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://webaim.org/projects/million/\"\u003eWebAIM Million Report\u003c/a\u003e exposed a sobering truth: Only 5.2% of the top million websites meet basic accessibility standards. The rest fail to meet current WCAG guidelines, as well as \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.section508.gov/\"\u003eSection 508\u003c/a\u003e and state governance in the U.S., and even tenets of the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://commission.europa.eu/strategy-and-policy/policies/justice-and-fundamental-rights/disability/european-accessibility-act-eaa_en\"\u003eEuropean Accessibility Act.\u003c/a\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith the rise of AI, there’s been a promise of meaningful impact at scale. Many see it as a salve, providing unprecedented automation and tooling to address wholesale errors like missing alt tags, ARIA labels, and other functional factors that trip up developers and content creators. With natural, human-like speech becoming a critical benefit of specific models – and ambient agents performing automated checks and remediation – AI stands to have a huge impact on accessibility.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut it’s not that simple. In my recent conversation with Lucy, we dug into this topic, exploring her concerns about communities with disabilities being overlooked in the AI wave. We discussed the positive traction and how certain aspects of AI hold real promise and potential, while specific products are already creating hesitation. We also talked WCAG, its pros and cons, and some of the legal ramifications. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen it comes to accessibility, we often focus on checking boxes and satisfying metrics in our tools. But as Lucy pointed out, there are real human considerations that get overlooked when we “customize ourselves out of accessibility.” This is why we need champions to advocate for change – and that’s exactly what she’s doing. \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"discovering-technology-as-a-fulcrum-for-change\"\u003eDiscovering technology as a fulcrum for change\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eBack in my agency days, I consulted with a company called \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_Scientific\"\u003eFreedom Scientific,\u003c/a\u003e a pioneer in the development of assistive computer technologies for blind and low-vision individuals. They have a line of accessible products, including software that enables screen magnification, reading, and the use of refreshable braille displays for modern devices. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ted_Henter\"\u003eTed Henter\u003c/a\u003e, one of the co-founders of Freedom Scientific, was a former motorcycle racer who became blind after a car accident. In the late 80s, he developed the company’s signature \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JAWS_(screen_reader)\"\u003eJAWS\u003c/a\u003e screen reader software, which became an industry staple. JAWS for Windows is just one of the many products that Lucy has cultivated a deep expertise with. She also works with \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.nvaccess.org/download/\"\u003eNVDA\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://nuancedragonsoftware.com/product/dragon-professional-v16/\"\u003eDragon Naturally Speaking,\u003c/a\u003e two highly respected platforms that offer accessible solutions. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLearning has long been a foundation of Lucy’s success. After pivoting from physical therapy, she pursued literature, which offered a pathway to other opportunities.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I went for my next big love, which was reading,” she recalled. “And I figured, I need a degree, because as a disabled person, getting a job without a degree at that time was just not possible.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003ch4 style=\"text-align:center\" id=\"-\"\u003e \u003c/h4\u003e\u003ch4 style=\"text-align:center\" id=\"“as-i-connected-with-other-people-with-disabilities,-i-tended-to-be-the-person-who-would-teach-them-how-to-use-computers.”\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cmark class=\"marker-yellow\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e“As I connected with other people with disabilities, I tended to be the person who would teach them how to use computers.”\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy discovered her love of computers in 1985. When she attended college, they were popping up everywhere on campus, and she realized how they could level the playing field for blind students. The timing was serendipitous – and the experience illuminating. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Personal computers were starting to become very, very popular,” she said. “And I was always an early adopter, because I loved playing with toys. Realizing that a computer could get me through anything that I had struggled with in college wasn’t just insightful, it was just completely liberating.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat early exposure to assistive technology built on Lucy’s natural proclivity to help others. The “bug” to teach technology started informally but later evolved into more formal programs. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“When I moved to the US, I started volunteering at a school for the blind, and trained people who couldn't get training in other places,” she explained. “As I connected with other people with disabilities, I tended to be the person who would teach them how to use computers.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA natural coach, Lucy brought real conviction to her early advocacy, upleveling skills and broadening opportunities for blind and disabled people. From simple things like budgeting in Quicken to getting through university courses, she has helped transform lives by sharing her knowledge. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis ultimately led to the founding of Access Aces in the early 2000s, which delivers presentations and training on topics like accessibility and disability awareness, as well as W3C evaluations and strategic accessibility plans.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut her work doesn't stop at the keyboard. Lucy is also a sounding board for consumer products, providing equipment reviews and how-to guides for the blind. She has an \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/@accessaces\"\u003eactive YouTube channel \u003c/a\u003ethat features “know before you buy” videos that assess the accessibility of devices and home appliances. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"media\"\u003e\u003cdiv data-oembed-url=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gGry7lB-I4U\"\u003e\u003cdiv style=\"position:relative;padding-bottom:100%;height:0;padding-bottom:56.2493%\"\u003e\u003ciframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/gGry7lB-I4U\" style=\"position:absolute;width:100%;height:100%;top:0;left:0\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; encrypted-media\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"transforming-lives-–-one-student-at-a-time\"\u003eTransforming lives – one student at a time\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor 20 years, Lucy worked at UC Berkeley in an assistive tech lab, helping students one-on-one and providing both technology guidance and deeply human problem-solving. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne heartfelt story she shared with me – about a grad student coming into her office one afternoon – captured both the stakes she faced and the potential of her impact.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I've never really been able to read,” Lucy recalled the young woman saying. “I've only been able to get through college as far as I have because my mother would read everything to me. But last year, she passed away, and I don't have the ability to read anymore.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAfter performing a quick spot assessment, Lucy set her up with reading software and loaded several options from her library of digitized books. She sat the student down at 10 AM, intending to check back soon – and then got distracted.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I went back to the room at the end of the day to clean up,” Lucy said. “It was about 5:30, and she was still sitting there at the computer. I'm like, ‘Are you okay? Is everything going well here?’ She turned around and burst into tears, telling me how she just read two of my textbooks. It was the first time she’d ever been able to read a book independently, to understand it, comprehend it, and gain information from it.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy described it as life-altering, and she has countless stories like this – stories of students who became doctors, business leaders, and technologists. Once they had tools that could actually work for them, it changed everything.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I had a student who was dyslexic and became a doctor,” Lucy said. “He taught his fellow doctors how to use Dragon [software] to document case notes, and he knew how to use it because I taught him while he was enrolled at the University.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy’s experiences underscore the impact of technology on people with disabilities and how the academic ecosystem has been transformed. Braille, for example, was once the central channel for blind literacy, but a wider range of form factors like screenreaders, audiobooks, and AI-driven accessibility tools are making it easier for students to excel. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://ablr360.com/the-importance-of-braille-in-a-technology-driven-world/\"\u003eAccording to Ablr,\u003c/a\u003e literacy comes in many forms, and humans learn in different ways. The real power lies in having options and choosing the tools that work best. This is where Lucy has focused on technology as a mechanism for changing lives.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"the-evolving-role-of-wcag-\"\u003eThe evolving role of WCAG \u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eOver time, Lucy’s work at UC Berkley evolved. What started as one-off fixes across a myriad of digital applications – specifically websites – scaled into a broader challenge of tackling system-wide accessibility barriers across the University. To meet this charter, she had a hand in shaping everything from procurement to product selection, and nurturing the culture with it. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It was the first time UC Berkley actually paid somebody to do accessibility work and do it at a systemic level,” she said. “Not student X needs this remediated for them, but more like all students could benefit from this website working better. For example, when we buy a system to help us create our course catalog, we make it accessible by default, instead of having students ask us to have it remediated for them.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne interesting thing that Lucy discussed is the role of the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.w3.org/WAI/standards-guidelines/wcag/\"\u003eWeb Content Accessibility Guidelines (WCAG)\u003c/a\u003e. Launched by the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.w3.org/\"\u003eW3C\u003c/a\u003e in 1998, it’s a set of international standards designed to ensure digital content is accessible to people with disabilities. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWCAG is built on four principles, often referred to as POUR: \u003ci\u003ePerceivable\u003c/i\u003e, \u003ci\u003eOperable\u003c/i\u003e, \u003ci\u003eUnderstandable\u003c/i\u003e, and \u003ci\u003eRobust\u003c/i\u003e. Based on how content scores within this matrix, WCAG applies a level of conformance (from lowest to highest: A, AA, or AAA) to websites, mobile experiences, and even document accessibility. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor website stakeholders – this includes everyone from designers to developers to content editors – the current WCAG 2.2 guidelines provide a foundation for accessibility by coding semantic HTML, using ARIA labels, and designing for accessibility from ground zero. As I’ve already mentioned, these pillars are often neglected, so compliance testing becomes a requirement using automated tools, manual keyboard checks, and screen reader tests. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhile WCAG provides some semblance of uniformity, it has long been viewed as a moving target, given that digital experiences evolve much faster than regulatory motions. And while some countries have passed accessibility laws – enforcing compliance much like the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.ada.gov/\"\u003eADA (Americans with Disabilities Act)\u003c/a\u003e enforces ramps in public buildings – others have not. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI asked Lucy where this all fits in the calculus. While she agreed that it’s essential to have a central body for policies, she admitted an increasing frustration with a “checklist mentality” around WCAG and the requirements of certain settlements. Her own methodology is driven by real people – and tasks that deliver tangible outcomes.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I don't focus on the W3C,” Lucy said. “I've never memorized the WCAG. It's a tool I have in my back pocket, sure, but what I focus on is how well can a person do what they need to do. When I consult for an organization, I'll say, ‘Tell me the three things you need somebody to do with this.’ Then I try to get them done as a screen reader user, or as a keyboard-only user, or someone who has to use an alternative input like speech recognition.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"a-frenetic-legal-landscape,-from-ada-to-eaa\"\u003eA frenetic legal landscape, from ADA to EAA\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy now, most digital experience practitioners are familiar with the legal implications of accessibility compliance. Here in the U.S., we’ve seen \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://gic.delaware.gov/consequences-of-accessibility-non-compliance/\"\u003epublic sector websites sued\u003c/a\u003e for a range of Title II and Section 508 accessibility issues over the years. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAdditionally, major brands like Target, Domino’s Pizza, and Netflix have been embroiled in \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.levelaccess.com/blog/title-iii-lawsuits-10-big-companies-sued-over-website-accessibility/\"\u003ehighly publicized, years-long litigation\u003c/a\u003e over basic functionality, closed-captioning, and other services that would enrich experiences for customers with disabilities. Some have been resolved. Others are ongoing – and much of that has to do with a lack of clarity. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhile the U.S. has struggled to back up digital accessibility with uniform policies, Europe is moving faster. This has been codified with the adoption of its landmark \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://commission.europa.eu/strategy-and-policy/policies/justice-and-fundamental-rights/disability/european-accessibility-act-eaa_en\"\u003eEuropean Accessibility Act (EAA).\u003c/a\u003e Lucy explained why this is a significant shift.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Europe is now requiring accessibility, and it’s going to cause a lot of change, just like it did with their data privacy act,” she said. “The US has never put teeth behind any of the rules they've made. Even with the ADA, somebody could be found in violation of a rule, and all they have to do is fix the thing. There's no actual penalty for violating it. So there's no incentive for them to be proactive. The incentive to do so doesn't happen until they get sued.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo address this gap, some EU member states are taking a much harder line. Ireland, for example, has a provision for potential jail time for serious non-compliance, along with some hefty fines.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLitigation is already beginning. In France, four major French grocery retailers – \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auchan\"\u003eAuchan\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.carrefour.com/en\"\u003eCarrefour\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.e.leclerc/\"\u003eE. Leclerc\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Picard_Surgel%C3%A9s\"\u003ePicard Surgelés\u003c/a\u003e – were all hit with legal action in July of 2025 for failing to comply with EAA standards. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs Lucy said, it’s no accident that major tech players are aligning with the EAA. Many of them operate on a global level, and the penalties aren’t just monetary. They’re reputational. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“When I do my work with big Silicon Valley companies here, I see them all panicking to meet the EAA,” she said. “My husband has worked on a device accessibility team for a major tech company. Everything he's done since he started there has been EAA-focused. I'm on the advisory board for Microsoft for their accessibility projects. Everything they're doing is focused on fixing EAA violations.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy has experienced these legal battles firsthand and fiercely advocated that responses be as compliant as possible. From her vantage point, companies and organizations often reach for the lowest rung of the ladder to satisfy a legal settlement – and that’s not always in the best interest of people with disabilities. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I'm all about usability and user experience and best practices,” she said, describing standards that brands arguably care about when it comes to every other user. But with \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.un.org/development/desa/disabilities/resources/factsheet-on-persons-with-disabilities.html\"\u003e16% of the global population experiencing a significant disability\u003c/a\u003e of some form – and an aging populace that is rapdily fall into that group – it’s a massively underrepresented segment. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFailing them isn’t just a moral shortcoming. It’s a missed opportunity. \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"why-accessibility-overlays-miss-the-mark\"\u003eWhy accessibility overlays miss the mark\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne thing that came up in our conversation was the growing pervasiveness of “one-line” digital accessibility tools like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://accessibe.com/\"\u003eaccessiBe\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://userway.org/\"\u003eUserway\u003c/a\u003e. This category of accessibility overlays and widgets has become a popular SaaS salve, in part because they’re relatively cheap – and they only require a single line of JavaScript to activate on any website frontend. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI asked Lucy about these products, and she didn’t mince words.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We have a huge division in the world of accessibility with those one-line of code overlays,” she said. “For many years, the biggest company that does that, if their tool was on a website, I could not actually \u003ci\u003euse\u003c/i\u003e the website. It would see that I was running a screen reader, and it would say, \u003ci\u003elet me help you. Here's my toolbar. Turn me on.\u003c/i\u003e I was like, ‘No, I don't want to do that.’ I'd hit ignore, but it would continue to draw my focus back. It went through and replaced alt text on all graphics, even if it had alt text already. It's just terrible stuff.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFrom my own experience, these plug-and-play tools are a panacea, and far from being a complete solution. In fact, experts warn that they can \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.accessibility.works/blog/accessibility-overlay-widgets-attract-lawsuits/\"\u003eonly detect about 30% to 40% of accessibility issues,\u003c/a\u003e and can’t address complex, context-dependent, or structural issues. On the legal side, they’re not the shield many organizations think they are.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Last year, there were hundreds of lawsuits filed specifically because they had that tool on them,” Lucy said. “Wow. And it just gets worse.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAccording to Lucy, some voices have suggested that accessibility professionals criticize overlays to protect their business interests. She said nothing could be further from the truth.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I don't know one person who's working in accessibility who wants to make work for ourselves,” she expressed vehemently. “I would rather be out of work or doing something else.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"the-promise-(and-peril)-of-ai-for-accessibility\"\u003eThe promise (and peril) of AI for accessibility\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAt the CMS Connect conference in Montreal last August, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/company/valtech/posts/?feedView=all\"\u003eValtech’s\u003c/a\u003e \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/allison-abraham-0b6212/\"\u003eAllison Abraham\u003c/a\u003e gave an inspiring presentation of an adaptive digital “AI concierge” for a major auto brand. She emphasized the “mighty forces” at play with AI, data, and cloud technologies, and how the shifting world of digital services can personalize experiences for consumers.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDespite these jaw-dropping advancements, Lucy asked a potent question about accessibility within the context of dynamically-generated AI content and experiences. \u003ci\u003eHow do we test it? Will accessibility tools work? Where are the gaps?\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUnfortunately, there wasn’t a good answer. And while AI has the potential to solve many challenges, there’s still work to be done to ensure inclusive experiences.  \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy is neither anti-AI nor naïve about it. She’s excited but wary of highly personalized, real‑time AI experiences that are effectively black boxes for users of assistive tech. Her underlying concern: if every interaction is dynamically generated, how do we ensure it remains navigable and understandable for people with disabilities?\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I love AI,” she told me. “I think it’s very powerful. But the problem is that we don't have an AI that's been trained on good accessibility data yet. It's all being trained on everything that's out there.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 style=\"text-align:center\" id=\"“i-love-ai.-i-think-it’s-very-powerful.-but-the-problem-is-that-we-don't-have-an-ai-that's-been-trained-on-good-accessibility-data-yet.-it's-all-being-trained-on-everything-that's-out-there.”-\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cmark class=\"marker-yellow\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e“I love AI. I think it’s very powerful. But the problem is that we don't have an AI that's been trained on good accessibility data yet. It's all being trained on everything that's out there.” \u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd as the WebAIM Million report established, almost \u003ci\u003eeverything\u003c/i\u003e out there fails accessibility. As such, we’re training AI on bad patterns at a massive scale, and the trust equation hasn't been solved – yet. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy also shared a particularly stark example of an AI-driven mobility device that detects and distinguishes between obstacles and people. It’s an example of how AI might be doing its job, but failing with the user experience.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I have a product I wear that’s supposed to help me avoid obstacles and people as I'm walking down the street,” she said. “If there's an obstacle in front of me, it starts making a weird clicking noise, and if there's a person, it makes a high-pitched tone. I can wear earbuds, but that is a horrifying experience to be walking down the street and hearing \u003ci\u003eclick, click, click\u003c/i\u003e. That's not effective, right?”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDespite those critiques, Lucy is quick to point out where AI is genuinely promising and even liberating. For her, that’s crystallized by advancements in \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://gopro.com/en/gs/shop/mounts-accessories/fluid-pro-ai/AGMSS-011.html\"\u003eAI-powered gimbals\u003c/a\u003e – camera stabilizers that use built-in algorithms and sensors to auto-track subjects, capture smooth footage, and enable hands-free operation. Using these capabilities, she can finally record video independently. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“There are a lot of gimbals on the market for phones and cameras, and the AI allows the gimbal to automatically pivot your camera to follow the subject,” she explained. “As a YouTube producer, I've always had to get my husband to point the camera for me, and he hates participating in my process. I recorded my last two videos without him having to point the camera. I gave the thing the hand gesture it requires, and the camera pivoted. It was beautiful.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe only problem? She said there’s no feedback for a blind user to know that the camera is tracking them. All it needed was a beep to indicate focus. It’s another example of not thinking through the accessibility lens in a product’s foundational design process. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eStill, this example is what gets her excited about the possibilities.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It’s the real promise of AI,” she said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"embracing-inclusion-by-design\"\u003eEmbracing inclusion by design\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAgain and again, Lucy brought us back to a central theme: \u003ci\u003eSolving accessibility is a people problem. \u003c/i\u003eTo achieve real outcomes, brands and organizations need to shift their cultural mindset, establish the right policies, and stand by them. Most importantly, she thinks hiring and empowering disabled professionals is the real activation point.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We're not going to fix it with tools,” she said. “We're going to fix it with people who understand that. And the way to do it is to invest in people with disabilities, bring them into your field and into your office space and work with them.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy also pointed out that this community is also the most underrepresented in the workforce. According to the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.bls.gov/news.release/disabl.nr0.htm\"\u003eU.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics,\u003c/a\u003e the unemployment rate for people with disabilities is twice that of the rest of the population (roughly 7.5%). \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFurther, in 2025, it cited that the employment-population ratio – the proportion of the population that is employed – was 22.7% among those with a disability. In contrast, the employment-population ratio for those without a disability was 65.5%. The chasm can't be ignored.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It’s a huge issue,” she said. “And these people can do the work. We're also some of the most educated. Most people with disabilities who have an education usually have three to five degrees, because they keep going back to school when they can't find a job. It's a sick cycle.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor developers and product teams, there are certainly opportunities for growth as regulation becomes fiercer. Last year, the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.ada.gov/resources/web-rule-first-steps/\"\u003eU.S. ADA passed the first requirements\u003c/a\u003e for most state and local government agencies to ensure their websites and mobile apps are accessible – a step in the right direction that will require significant support. But Lucy also sees an intrinsic personal benefit in all of this.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“People who end up working on accessibility after they've learned about it find their work so much more rewarding,” she said. “You could be a web coder for decades, and if all of a sudden, you learn that your code wasn't working for 25% of the population, and then you figure out how to make your code work for them? You can get a huge adrenaline rush from that.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"where-accessibility-goes-next\"\u003eWhere accessibility goes next\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eLucy’s story isn’t neat. Or linear. It’s full of setbacks and challenges. But it’s also been inspiring and illuminating – crystallized by a moment when a college student with disabilities realizes they can read for the first time. That was a powerful testament to the work she’s done throughout her career and the immeasurable impact she’s had on her community. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor her next act, Lucy is doubling down on teaching and sharing. As she transitions out of her day-to-day (what she loosely calls “retirement”), her goal is to telegraph her wisdom through speaking opportunities and across communities. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I want to speak at as many conferences and as many events as possible to teach people about accessibility, so that they can experience that same adrenaline rush, that feeling of knowing that the work they’re doing is actually \u003ci\u003eworth\u003c/i\u003e something.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor those of us shaping the CMS and digital experience ecosystem – especially in an AI‑driven world – there’s a powerful invitation in all of this. A call to build richer teams and more inclusive products, where people with disabilities aren’t edge cases but co-creators. Vendors like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://kontent.ai/\"\u003eKontent.ai\u003c/a\u003e are even partnering with organizations like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://kontent.ai/blog/author/zaneta-styblova/\"\u003eScope\u003c/a\u003e, a disability equality charity, to enhance their platform accessibility and ensure their headless CMS is usable for people with disabilities.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAgentic AI is reshaping every facet of our software, and we're seeing great use cases for addressing accessibility. This year alone, I've participated in multiple demos where AI agents work ambiently in the background to perform accessibility checks and remediate issues. It's impressive. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut as the growth of co-pilots and vibe coding makes software development easier, faster, and less expensive – and agents are being tasked with more responsibility – there’s a growing risk that accessibility will become an assumption, or once again, just another box to check. That could be a recipe for failure. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs Lucy said, AI is a solution, but it's also being trained on our problems. The only sustainable path is one where people with disabilities are at the table from the beginning – designing, building, training, and governing the systems that will define how we experience the web in the years ahead. As such, we should strive to culturally embed accessibility and inclusion into the very core of our models, interfaces, and systems.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd yes, we need humans to continue this fight for inclusion. Smart practitioners with diverse backgrounds and experiences. Champions that can lead the charge to digital equality.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBecause people are the real heart – and the real heroes – of this story. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"upcoming-events\"\u003eUpcoming Events\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg style=\"width:34.15%\" src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/01/logo_jday_hor.png\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"joomladay-usa-2026\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.jdayusa.com/\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003eJoomlaDay USA 2026\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eApril 29 - May 2, 2026 – Delray Beach, Florida\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBe part of the Joomla community in one of the most iconic cities in the world! Greco","id":"5de74180-1118-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","slug":"lucy-greco","wordpressId":null,"postTagJoin":{"PostId":"f2766e40-1111-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"5de74180-1118-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae"}},{"name":"Accessibility","id":"0e50d530-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"accessibility","wordpressId":"126","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"f2766e40-1111-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"0e50d530-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}},{"name":"Digital Accessibility","id":"b23fea10-1396-11ef-b4c7-c92038bb686f","slug":"digital-accessibility","wordpressId":null,"postTagJoin":{"PostId":"f2766e40-1111-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"b23fea10-1396-11ef-b4c7-c92038bb686f"}},{"name":"W3C","id":"13a434a0-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"w3c","wordpressId":"147","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"f2766e40-1111-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"13a434a0-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}},{"name":"wcag","id":"13a482c0-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"wcag","wordpressId":"250","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"f2766e40-1111-11f1-9541-3d9dddbe6eae","TagId":"13a482c0-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}}],"postProduct":null,"campaignPost":null,"minutesToRead":21},{"name":"Websites Still Rock: Kentico’s 2025 ‘Site of the Year’ Winners Push the Boundaries of Digital Experience ","intro":"From migrations with AI-driven tools to upgrades with full UX redesign, Kentico is spotlighting the excellence and innovation of its partners and customers as they build the future on Xperience by Kentico.","content":"\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor anyone in the website business, building something beautiful is literally the top of the mountain. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eYou know what I mean. There’s nothing more satisfying than designing, coding, and pushing a project into production – then seeing a bump in traffic, an increase in performance, and a wave of adoration across social media. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut adding an award to your mantle? That just takes it to the next level. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/products/kentico\"\u003eKentico\u003c/a\u003e, celebrating these efforts is a big point of pride, especially for a platform that powers over 90,000 websites across the globe. For almost a decade, the DXP has highlighted the very best work of its partners and clients with its coveted \u003cstrong\u003e“Site of the Year” Awards\u003c/strong\u003e – and they just released the winners of its 2025 edition.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/kentico-announces-winners-of-2023-site-of-the-year-awards\"\u003eI’ve covered this program\u003c/a\u003e previously, and I’m always impressed by the quality, complexity, and bold ambition of the finalists. 2025’s crop once again demonstrates the daring and prowess of organizations and their partners to push the boundaries and redefine modern digital experiences built on \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.kentico.com/CMSModules/Newsletters/CMSPages/Redirect.ashx?linkguid=11b4f14a-807d-4840-bfa8-e529c85898b7\u0026amp;email=matt%40cmscritic.com\u0026amp;hash=be0d1d8f19e0858f5111492f222eca952b1f9d98aaaeebe1c4c04b9dec830ced\"\u003eXperience by Kentico\u003c/a\u003e –\u003cspan style=\"color:#30313D\"\u003e \u003c/span\u003ethe multichannel content management, marketing, and digital commerce solution packaged in one cohesive platform.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis year’s class showed up with some stunning, full-scale UX redesigns that deliver visual awe and impact. But there were feats of engineering as well, with a myriad of use cases featuring AI-powered marketing transformations and complex workload migrations.  \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eKentico’s “Site of the Year” program is categorized by industry, spanning wide cohorts like B2B as well as verticals in financial services, commerce, education, hospitality, healthcare, government, and NGOs. 2025's submissions came from across the planet, including North America, EMEA, and APAC – illustrating the flexibility and extensibility of Xperience by Kentico.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn addition to these examples of partner and customer-driven excellence, 2025 was a big year of milestones for Kentico. With global demand growing for it signature platform, the company’s continued investment in AI was crystallized by \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.kentico.com/platform/aira\"\u003ethe launch of AIRA\u003c/a\u003e (Artificial Intelligence Recommendations \u0026amp; Assistance), a native AI agent that unpacks and understands content and customer data to help streamline the creation, optimization, and time to deploy for digital experiences. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBuilding on its AIRA momentum, Kentico is once again aiming to transform expectations in 2026. The company recently introduced its \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/introducing-the-agentic-marketing-suite-kentico-extends-its-ai-strategy-to-power-marketing-teams\"\u003eAgentic Marketing Suite,\u003c/a\u003e extending its AI strategy to power teams with specialized agents, each designed to execute marketing and content tasks that unlock operational efficiencies in team workflows. \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"honoring-creativity-and-innovation\"\u003eHonoring creativity and innovation\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eLet’s talk about websites – because they’re still the center of gravity. More than ever, the world’s leading brands rely on unique, high-performing digital experiences across multiple channels, hoping to dazzle visitors and convert interest into action. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eEven amidst the shifts in traffic and the rise of AI-powered answer engines, smart consumers still value a business’s website as a central source of truth. At the same time, websites are essential to arming the new frontier of GEO and AEO by delivering a foundation of well-structured content.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eKentico’s “Site of the Year” honors its clients and partners by focusing a spotlight on their remarkable work – websites and digital solutions that achieve the highest levels of creativity, innovation, content strategy, and technological implementation.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eA bit of level-setting on the rules:\u003c/strong\u003e Only projects that first earned Kentico’s “Site of the Month” banner were eligible to compete, making these finalists a true “best of the best” compendium. Winners were selected by an internal Kentico judging committee based on overall excellence and measurable impact.\u003cspan style=\"color:#4F4C4D\"\u003e  \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eYou can explore more about this \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.kentico.com/CMSModules/Newsletters/CMSPages/Redirect.ashx?linkguid=18b8acaa-24af-4f10-976e-74ebe1bf15e4\u0026amp;email=matt%40cmscritic.com\u0026amp;hash=be0d1d8f19e0858f5111492f222eca952b1f9d98aaaeebe1c4c04b9dec830ced\"\u003eyear’s winners and honorable mentions\u003c/a\u003e on Kentico’s website, where they drill into the details. For each category winner, they provide a well-rounded rationale that showcases the innovative thinking, stellar design, and AI-enhanced solutions that put them in the top spot.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you’re interested, you can also vote in Kentico’s \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/posts/kenticosoftware_communitychoice-soty-digitalexperience-activity-7429873612603596800-ltb5/?utm_source=share\u0026amp;utm_medium=member_desktop\u0026amp;rcm=ACoAABkGfZEBzxXaDBwgLBqINaYG9q1JUbfxMW8\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCommunity Choice Awards\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/a\u003e through March 6th. This crowdsourced portion of the program is handled entirely on LinkedIn.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWithout further ado…\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"2025-‘site-of-the-year’-winners-and-honorable-mentions----\"\u003e2025 ‘Site of the Year’ Winners and Honorable Mentions    \u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eMan, this was a dynamite grouping of sites – and all deserving of kudos. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor me, there were certainly some standouts. In the \u003ci\u003eB2B\u003c/i\u003e category, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.kentico.com/CMSModules/Newsletters/CMSPages/Redirect.ashx?linkguid=2352b3f4-ad18-4695-b4cf-9fea119232c4\u0026amp;email=matt%40cmscritic.com\u0026amp;hash=be0d1d8f19e0858f5111492f222eca952b1f9d98aaaeebe1c4c04b9dec830ced\"\u003eLeShuttle Freight’s\u003c/a\u003e elegant, high-performance, multilingual experience was top-notch. In addition to simple, intuitive navigation, it has a tricked-out, real-time service update that provides critical visibility for time-sensitive logistics. The mobile experience is also lightweight, prioritizing the right elements in the UX. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eImplemented by \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.crafted.co.uk/services/digital-products/kentico\"\u003eCrafted\u003c/a\u003e, a long-standing U.K.-based Kentico partner, LeShuttle is a solid design that streamlines the customer journey for logistics partners, drivers, and customers – so they can keep truckin'.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771964387975.png\" alt=\"\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eSource: LeShuttle Freight website\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn the \u003ci\u003eEntertainment, Hospitality, and Tourism\u003c/i\u003e category, I was also keen on the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://bobw.co/\"\u003eBob W. site\u003c/a\u003e, which made me want to book my next trip to Amsterdam today. The gestalt was right up my alley, offering a clean, minimal design with clear pathways to explore short-stay apartments in a variety of locales. Agency partner \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.idhlagency.com/\"\u003eIDHL\u003c/a\u003e did yeoman’s work on developing the “Bob” identity and persona, delivering a charming and inviting vibe to the experience. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAlong with some killer frontend features like smart filtering and a little backend magic with reusable content, Bob W. personifies what great UX is – and I love how it all supports a corporate commitment to sustainability and a stay that’s 100% offset. It’s hospitality that's more hospitable to the earth. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:90.66%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771964386776.png\" alt=\"\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eSource: Bob W. website\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo say that \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.kentico.com/CMSModules/Newsletters/CMSPages/Redirect.ashx?linkguid=d26dfe6c-b389-43aa-a623-daa701b4b192\u0026amp;email=matt%40cmscritic.com\u0026amp;hash=be0d1d8f19e0858f5111492f222eca952b1f9d98aaaeebe1c4c04b9dec830ced\"\u003eOppenheimer\u003c/a\u003e made a “bold” move to Kentico would be an understatement. As the winner in the \u003ci\u003eFinancial Services\u003c/i\u003e category, the wealth management leader successfully migrated from CrownPeak in only five months, with the goal of optimizing their content ops via single-source content management across multiple digital channels.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eImplemented by Kentico partner \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://sagepath-reply.com/\"\u003eSagepath Reply\u003c/a\u003e, Oppenheimer’s slick design captures the essence of a trusted financial partner while simplifying navigation to key topics like capital markets. They also introduced new AI-driven tools focused on marketing and content optimization. It feels powerful yet approachable – and evokes confidence and stability at every turn. For a financial institution, this was a winning investment.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771964386955.png\" alt=\"A close-up of a website\n\nAI-generated content may be incorrect.\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eSource: Oppenheimer website\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"winners-by-category\"\u003eWinners By Category\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"b2b\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eB2B\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWinner:\u003c/strong\u003e LeShuttle Freight (Implemented by Crafted)\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHonorable Mentions:\u003c/strong\u003e ZAG Interactive (ZAG Interactive), Westport (ALYKA Pty Ltd) \u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"commerce\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eCommerce\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWinner:\u003c/strong\u003e Translink (MSQ DX)\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHonorable Mentions:\u003c/strong\u003e Rhythm Japan (Interesting Solutions), Elkov Elektro (Bluesoft) \u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"consumer-goods-and-services\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eConsumer Goods and Services\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWinner:\u003c/strong\u003e MND Energie (Bluesoft)\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHonorable Mentions:\u003c/strong\u003e Best Best \u0026amp; Associations\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWinner:\u003c/strong\u003e American Society of Landscape Architects (BlueModus)\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eHonorable Mentions:\u003c/strong\u003e National Association of Independent Schools (ByteMinds), Eat Pecans (Rise, a Quad Agency) \u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"setting-new-standards-for-excellence\"\u003eSetting new standards for excellence\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eEach year, I’m asked to judge awards programs, so I’m accustomed to seeing amazing work. What I love about these competitions is that I’m always surprised, intrigued, and often floored by the creativity. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you’re embarking on a brand or digital transformation quest, finding the right agency partner is critical to success. But harnessing the right CMS or DXP at the foundation is equally as important – and awards programs like Kentico’s “Site of the Year” are a great place to window shop the possibilities. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis 2025 crop is a testament to the full potential of Xperience by Kentico. It’s not just about breathtaking UX, it’s also about leveraging a future-ready digital ecosystem to power multi-channel experiences across devices, languages, locations, and more. From hybrid headless implementations to secure member portals and complex third-party integrations, organizations are using the platform to unify content, marketing, and commerce into a single solution. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs Kentico continues to invest in a steady stream of innovation, its partners and clients will be the first beneficiaries to access new features. Case in point: Kentico’s new Agentic Marketing Suite is ushering in a new era of intelligent orchestration, helping marketers automate decisions, personalize journeys, and optimize campaigns at scale. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDigital experiences are no longer static. They continue to evolve – and so do our expectations. Even as websites morph into agentic experiences that serve both humans and bots, only people can be inspired by a brand's imagination and storytelling.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eKentico’s “Site of the Year” reminds us that websites still have this power and potential. When a\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.contentstack.com/blog/all-about-headless/cms-change-management-best-practices-for-seamless-enterprise-implementation\"\u003e \u003c/a\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.contentstack.com/blog/all-about-headless/cms-change-management-best-practices-for-seamless-enterprise-implementation?utm_campaign=\u0026amp;utm_medium=paid-affiliate\u0026amp;utm_source=cms-critic\u0026amp;utm_content=smarter-content-management-with-an-ai-cms\"\u003emodern CMS is implemented with proper change management\u003c/a\u003e practices to support its adoption, it also supports better governance, data-driven optimization, and automation. Here are other benefits.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFaster content creation and delivery\u003c/strong\u003e: AI authors’ workflows, ensuring faster editing. It applies the brand’s guidelines, eliminating human errors. Also, its automated tagging, categorization, and metadata generation feature ensures you can publish faster.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSmarter personalization at scale\u003c/strong\u003e: An AI CMS tracks data in real-time and adjusts content for relevant audience segments. Delivering on-brand content ensures you can convert more and engage your audience better.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMore efficient search and content discovery\u003c/strong\u003e: Search and discovery feature powered by conversational AI enables editors and marketers find content quickly, even in large, complex repositories.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eData-driven optimization\u003c/strong\u003e: An AI CMS also supports predictive content performance insights, enabling teams to be proactive.\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImproved compliance and governance\u003c/strong\u003e: An AI-powered CMS can flag missing disclosures, ensure accessibility standards, and apply consistent terminology.\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"how-ai-is-transforming-content-management-within-enterprise-cms\"\u003eHow AI is transforming content management within enterprise CMS\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI integration into content workflows goes beyond using generative AI to create content. It can be applied in other areas, such as SEO, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.contentstack.com/resources/report/enterprise-ai-search-playbook?utm_campaign=\u0026amp;utm_medium=paid-affiliate\u0026amp;utm_source=cms-critic\u0026amp;utm_content=smarter-content-management-with-an-ai-cms\"\u003eAIO/GEO\u003c/a\u003e, personalization, and predictive analytics. Here are some of those ways.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"content-intelligence-for-planning\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eContent intelligence for planning\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI scans competitor content, search queries, and your own content library. That allows you to identify gaps and opportunities in your content strategy and that of your competitors. Based on that insight, AI can also suggest high-performing topics, and align new content with buyer journeys, so content production supports pipeline and sales goals.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"ai-assisted-content-creation-and-editing\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAI-assisted content creation and editing\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith generative AI, you can generate content drafts, outlines and briefs. The AI is trained on your company’s audience persona, style guide and brand voice — hence, it can enforce the right tone of voice and style across your content.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"automated-content-tagging-and-classification\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAutomated content tagging and classification\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI-powered DAMs integrated in an intelligent CMS can scan your assets and suggest tags. It can further map those assets into your enterprise taxonomy, ensuring your assets fit into a structured content model. By doing so, marketers can easily search and reuse content.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"personalization-at-scale\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePersonalization at Scale\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt is no secret that enterprise customers prioritize brands that deliver tailored, one-to-one experiences. You can integrate a real-time CDP to track customer data and create profiles. Then, use an AI-powered CMS to analyze the data and recommend the most relevant content. That way, you can tailor experiences to different accounts, industries or decision-makers.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"seo-and-aio-optimization-support\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eSEO and AIO optimization support\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI can analyze search intent and suggest relevant keywords, topics and FAQs. It can be used to find internal linking opportunities, write meta titles and create schema markup. In essence, it becomes your SEO/AIO co-pilot, enabling you to find opportunities, match content to audience persona and optimize existing content.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"knowledge-assistant-for-internal-teams\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eKnowledge assistant for internal teams\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eInternal teams can also deploy AI-powered search and Q\u0026amp;A over enterprise content libraries. That way, teams within the organizations, such as sales and product teams, can quickly find answers backed by approved sources.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"governance-and-compliance-guardrails\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eGovernance and compliance guardrails\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI can be deployed to manage policy and style enforcement, as well as regulatory compliance checks. AI guardrails act like a compliance officer inside your CMS. By doing so, it prevents risky or off-brand content from being published. It also ensures that assets are safe, accurate and ready for regulation.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"governance,-security,-and-compliance-in-an-ai-cms\"\u003eGovernance, security, and compliance in an AI CMS\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI CMS platforms automate governance and security processes. However, team leaders still need to set approval workflows that AI should follow. They must apply built-in permissions to allow access to specific authorized users who can check and approve AI outputs.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe CMS offers intelligent security that can flag suspicious usage and trigger reminders for compliance audits. Still, content teams must keep to data privacy and safety regulations, such as GDPR and CCPA. They must also verify AI-generated metadata and tags to ensure compliance requirements are met and use audit logs to track changes made by AI features.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image-style-align-center image_resized\" style=\"width:83.96%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://images.contentstack.io/v3/assets/blt7359e2a55efae483/blt49eb52225d026692/68a9891e5075c355e79fb708/image.png\" alt=\"AI CMS features compared to a traditional CMS\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"ai-integrations-that-transform-content-workflows\"\u003eAI integrations that transform content workflows\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAn intelligent CMS supports AI integration, and that goes beyond automation. It makes your workflows smarter, so you can produce and publish content with more consistency and speed. Here are specific AI integrations that enable that.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003eAutomated AI tagging and categorization\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eAI-powered search and discovery\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eAutomated metadata generation\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003eAutomated A/B testing for content variants\u003cbr /\u003e \u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese features enable enterprises to reduce repetitive work and focus teams on high-impact, creative and strategic tasks.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-big\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cmark class=\"marker-yellow\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eFast-track digital experiences with Contentstack\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-big\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eNeed to create digital experiences quickly? Contentstack's content and editorial engine enables you to reach new markets and create digital experiences faster. Manage content with ease and speed. \u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.contentstack.com/try-for-free?utm_campaign=\u0026amp;utm_medium=paid-affiliate\u0026amp;utm_source=cms-critic\u0026amp;utm_content=smarter-content-management-with-an-ai-cms\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-big\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eStart your free trial today\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-big\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e.\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"comparing-ai-cms-options\"\u003eComparing AI CMS options\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eMost CMS platforms now embed some sort of AI integration or service. So, you have a backend that you can connect to any front-end framework via APIs. An AI CMS is a CMS with built-in AI integration to automate and enhance content creation, personalization, and management.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"is-an-ai-cms-secure-for-enterprise-use?\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eIs an AI CMS secure for enterprise use?\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eAn AI CMS is considered secure if it features enterprise-grade security, role-based permissions, audit logging, and compliance capabilities. The security of an intelligent CMS also depends on how AI integrations are configured and whether they comply with privacy laws.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"what-skills-do-teams-need-to-work-with-an-ai-cms?\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWhat skills do teams need to work with an AI CMS?\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003eContent teams should understand content strategy, governance rules, and how to review AI outputs for accuracy and compliance. Technical teams may need to understand AI prompts, workflow automation, and how to manage AI integrations.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"learn-more\"\u003eLearn more\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAI CMS platforms are redefining enterprise content management.
