Tale of Two Phils: Exploring Umbraco’s Open Source Vision for AI, MCP, and the Agentic Future of CMS","intro":"In the latest episode of “The Critic’s Corner” podcast, we chat with two of the key voices shaping the future of Umbraco: CTO Filip Bech-Larsen and AI Staff Engineer Phil Whittaker. What unfolds is a wide-ranging, candid, and forward-looking conversation about how a famously “Friendly CMS” is approaching AI, MCP, and the emerging agentic landscape. ","content":"\u003ch4 id=\"-\"\u003e \u003c/h4\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"listen-to-the-full-episode-of-“the-critic's-corner”-podcast-\u0026gt;\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/a-tale-of-two-phils-exploring-umbracos-open/id1801794414?i=1000749874476\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eListen to the full episode of “The Critic's Corner” Podcast \u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:rgb(77,153,230)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTwo Phils. Two origin stories. And one open source platform that’s trying to do something very intentional in this noisy AI era. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe platform I speak of is \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/products/umbraco\"\u003eUmbraco\u003c/a\u003e, a Denmark-based CMS with a .NET heritage and two decades of history under its belt. On CMS Critic, we’ve watched it grow and evolve over the years. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNow, as AI crushes roadmaps and stampedes with change, Umbraco is proving once more just how flexible and resilient its technology and community really are.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI was prepared to have a lively conversation with \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/filipbech/\"\u003eCTO Filip Bech-Larsen,\u003c/a\u003e whom I’ve spoken to frequently, about a slew of topics related to Umbraco’s AI roadmap – namely, its deep focus on \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://modelcontextprotocol.io/docs/getting-started/intro\"\u003eMCP (Model Context Protocol).\u003c/a\u003e The company is doubling down on this critical component as a key activator in its AI and agentic strategy, along with the recent unveiling of \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://github.com/umbraco/Umbraco.AI\"\u003eUmbraco.AI\u003c/a\u003e and the full availability of \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://umbraco.com/products/umbraco-compose/\"\u003eUmbraco Compose\u003c/a\u003e. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhat’s clear is that Umbraco's pace of innovation hasn’t slowed.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eKnown in many circles as \"The Friendly CMS,” perhaps it's apropos that Filip brought a friend to our call – a smart one who just happens to have the same name (OK, so they're \u003ci\u003eslightly\u003c/i\u003e different). As such, you get a bonus “Phil” on this episode: \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/phil-whittaker-82481716/\"\u003ePhil Whittaker.\u003c/a\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA long-time Umbraco community member and certified platform champion, Phil \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/umbraco-accelerates-ai-transformation-by-appointing-senior-software-engineer-to-focus-on-mcp\"\u003ejoined the company late last year\u003c/a\u003e as a Staff Engineer with the explicit directive of supporting the company’s AI and MCP transformation. He brought even more context to the conversation through his own technical lens. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image-style-align-center image_resized\" style=\"width:75.68%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771273158818.png\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eSee? Two Phils are better than one. From top left, clockwise: Matt Garrepy, Phil Whittaker, and Filip Bech-Larsen\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn the pod, Filip and Phil shared their parallel journeys to Umbraco, elevated by a common belief that the real power lies not just in the product, but in a collaborative ecosystem where people can share ideas and solve problems. Together, they unpacked how Umbraco is staying true to its open values while still pushing into the next era of AI innovation.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe also discussed Umbraco’s two-speed innovation model: a stable, predictable core that enterprises can depend on, and a fast-moving marketplace where partners and the community experiment with AI add-ons, agent workflows, and automation patterns. This approach aims to reduce “AI whiplash” while still delivering practical value for marketers and developers – especially around harder problems like context, experimentation, and personalization.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you care about the intersection of CMS, AI, and the open web, this episode will “Phil” you up. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIs it DRY or redundant? Anything but.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"media\"\u003e\u003cdiv data-oembed-url=\"https://youtu.be/7IlSNXErLpc\"\u003e\u003cdiv style=\"position:relative;padding-bottom:100%;height:0;padding-bottom:56.2493%\"\u003e\u003ciframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/7IlSNXErLpc\" style=\"position:absolute;width:100%;height:100%;top:0;left:0\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; encrypted-media\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"parallel-origin-stories-converge-with-“the-friendly-cms”\"\u003eParallel origin stories converge with “The Friendly CMS”\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eBoth Filip and Phil came to Umbraco the same way many people do: as accomplished builders. Along their own unique paths, they pushed the limits of creativity – notching successes and facing failure. Along the way, they discovered the power and inclusivity of Umbraco’s community.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor Filip, the exploration began decades ago as a young, ambitious developer. After experimenting with his own custom CMS project, he had an “aha” moment after attending Umbraco's annual \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/sowing-the-seeds-of-love-umbracos-codegarden-2025-celebrates-20-years-of-community-and-innovation\"\u003eCodegarden event.\u003c/a\u003e That shaped his view of what was possible with an open source CMS – and a passionate community behind to it.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I went to my first Codegarden, more than 10 years ago now, and I just fell in love with the product and the community,” he recalled. “It was love at first sight.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor Phil, the story shares a kinship. Like Filip, he tried to crack his own CMS code about 20 years ago. Ultimately, those efforts led him to the agency side of the development game, where he moved from pure .NET development into content design. That’s where he first encountered Umbraco.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I started to really get a love for content design and content modeling and all those types of elements that developers really shouldn’t get involved in,” he said, laughing. “But I started to really enjoy it and really get on with it.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBoth Filip and Phil have anchored their respective stories in Umbraco’s community ethos, describing it as something much more than just a collection of connected builders. For both of them, it runs much deeper. According to Filip, this is why the company still embraces the moniker of “The Friendly CMS” across its branding.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It feels like a big family, really, and that’s amazing,” Phil said. \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"open-source,-transparency,-and-the-umbraco-ethos\"\u003eOpen Source, transparency, and the Umbraco ethos\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eFrom the beginning, Umbraco’s identity has been defined by its flexibility, openness, and a clear commitment to democratizing the web. Adopting an open source foundation in 2005, just after the Umbraco 2.0 release, wasn’t an afterthought – it reflected a conscious pulse that pumped triumphantly through the culture. These are tenets that Filip has long subscribed to and continues to champion in his vision as CTO.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Umbraco has always been about flexibility and being able to do just what you want and how you want, and Umbraco was just there to help you and to quickly get out of your way,” he said. “I love the philosophy of open source and democratizing publishing on the web. It still makes my heartbeat. That’s what it’s all about: making it for everybody.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eLater in the episode, Filip connected that ethos directly to how Umbraco thinks about AI and its overall platform strategy. Transparency, he argues, should extend to AI choices as well – and that means not locking customers into a vendor-defined AI stack. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We want to be completely transparent about our plans so you can make the best decisions,” he said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"mcp-as-a-“pick-and-mix”-toolset-for-agentic-ai\"\u003eMCP as a “pick and mix” toolset for agentic AI\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs mentioned, a big thrust for Umbraco’s AI strategy is MCP, and this is precisely where Phil has been targeting his technical prowess and creativity. I’ve been covering the evolution of MCP going back to early 2024, when a few examples were emerging in areas like agentic commerce. Today, there are thousands of MCP servers available across a wide range of ecosystems.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHere’s a quick refresher, just in case you’re not familiar: MCP is an open source standard for connecting AI applications to external systems, enabling AI apps like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://claude.ai/\"\u003eClaude\u003c/a\u003e or \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://chatgpt.com/\"\u003eChatGPT\u003c/a\u003e to connect to data sources, tools, and workflows to access information and perform tasks.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:82.44%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771272780349.png\" alt=\"A diagram of a standard protocol\n\nAI-generated content may be incorrect.\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eSource: modelcontextprotocol.io\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://dust.tt/blog/mcp-and-enterprise-agents-building-the-ai-operating-system-for-work\"\u003eAnthropic\u003c/a\u003e, the company that originally pioneered the protocol, has described MCP as the “USB‑C of agentic tooling,” which is an appropriate analogy. But Phil offers a more vivid and perhaps actionable metaphor through the Umbraco lens.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I see it as a ‘pick and mix,’” he said. “So what you’re doing is laying out your stall of tools, and the agent can pick and choose which ones it wants to use to complete whatever it is you’ve asked it to do.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor a complex product like Umbraco, that’s powerful. According to Phil, MCP allows “magic” to happen, letting you compose different agents to complete tasks that were previously impossible to do. And they’re already seeing real-world use cases from developers.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It’s like the keys to all of Umbraco, right?” he said. “People are starting to pick up MCP now and use it in an implementation and production capacity. They’re able to use it and combine it with other elements within their MCP platform, things \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/products/figma\"\u003eFigma\u003c/a\u003e, and really accelerate what they’re doing and how quickly they can move. This is what allows agents to work with our platform.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"owning-the-ai-strategy\"\u003eOwning the AI strategy\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eA recurring theme in the conversation is who should own the AI strategy. For Filip, the answer is clear – and it’s bolstered by a foundational understanding of where your “superpowers” exist. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We want you to be in charge of your own AI strategy,” he said. “We want to focus on content management, because that’s what we’re really good at, and we have years of experience and a proven platform.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFilip was explicit about the risk of vendor-dictated AI, and why enterprises and organizations should carefully and thoughtfully choose the AI solution that’s the best fit for their needs – and that doesn’t necessarily come from the same place as your CMS. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Don’t tie your AI strategy to your CMS or to your PIM or to whatever,” he said. “Find the AI strategy that works for your enterprise. Don’t be forced into using one model over the other just because that’s what your vendor chose for you.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThere’s a clear composable thread to all of this, and Filip reinforced where it aligns with the open spirit of Umbraco. MCP helps make the possibilities of choice more practical by standardizing the bridge between Umbraco and the growing field of models, agents, and other dimensions of a customer's AI preferences.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"a-two-speed-strategy:-stable-core,-fast-ecosystem\"\u003eA two-speed strategy: Stable core, fast ecosystem\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne of the things we spoke about in the pod was Umbraco’s solution for balancing stability with the breakneck pace of AI. With change being a weekly or even a daily constant, Filip described a sort of “two-speed” innovation model that supports their success. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis has very real architectural and experimental implications. At one end of the spectrum, it’s about being methodical and stable with AI. That’s balanced by Umbraco’s marketplace of ideas, which acts as a kind of accelerator – a bleeding-edge intersection where the ecosystem can support everyone. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“It’s very important to us that we’re predictable, and we don’t add something that we need to remove later,” he explained. “So we’re intentionally a little bit slow on this, on putting [AI] inside of the core product itself. But there are a few open source things in our marketplace for AI, and there are commercial products out there. With that dual kind of strategy, fast and slow, we get the best of both worlds.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003ePhil also zeroed in on the overall flexibility of Umbraco to meet the expanding needs of AI, which is buoyed by its solid foundation. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“When you break it down, Umbraco is a series of tools to build on top of, and that’s always been our power,” he said. “It’s very extensible and very easy to build stuff on top of it, especially in this agentic world.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"the-umbraco-community-as-a-force-multiplier\"\u003eThe Umbraco community as a force multiplier\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eWithout question, one of the jewels in Umbraco’s open source crown is its highly engaged community. Boasting more than \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://umbraco.com/about-us\"\u003e250,000 developers and users,\u003c/a\u003e it's also nurturing a well-established global network of digital agencies. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUmbraco’s ecosystem has already been a wellspring for AI innovation, with numerous third-party packages available via its \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://marketplace.umbraco.com/category/artificial-intelligence\"\u003eUmbraco Marketplace\u003c/a\u003e. Builders can access everything from content generation to image manipulation, search optimization to translation. For example, plugins like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://umbraco.allyy.io/\"\u003eAllyy.io\u003c/a\u003e help extend functionality with AI, enabling users to enhance their website with personalized content recommendations.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:80.53%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771272780363.png\" alt=\"A screenshot of a computer\n\nAI-generated content may be incorrect.\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eSource: Umbraco Marketplace website\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eUmbraco’s community is a clear asset to its AI horizon, and Filip sees this charter evolving. As he told me during the podcast, they used to host community hackathons to help fix bugs in the CMS. Now that the platform is exceedingly stable, these events are focusing on MCP and AI scenarios – and pushing the boundaries of where things can go. This is creating sparks of innovation.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“When we do hackathons, we take a full day and get everybody working with our MCP to see what they come up with,” he said. “It’s actually pretty good at writing Umbraco code with a little bit of instruction and access to the MCP server.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe other part of the equation is partners, which, according to Filip, are still the primary go-to-market channel. As he said, all of these community-focused initiatives are about enriching relationships, elevating awareness, and upleveling skills. The goal is to make this cabal of builders more efficient, so they can translate the value of Umbraco to the end customer.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne thing Filip keyed in on was the air of “competitive camaraderie” that exists in the community. Even though many partner agencies might find themselves vying for the same RFPs, there’s a cooperative sensibility that exists – a mindset of elevating the Umbraco tides and lifting their collective ships.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“There’s really this ethos at Umbraco that we share ideas,” he said. “You might be in competition over a specific customer project, and then the next day, the same people will be on the forum and discussing ideas and growing the business of Umbraco together.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003ePhil sees another benefit to this collaboration: helping partners keep up with the pace of AI. “Because this is moving so quickly, I’m trying to help partners,” he said. This is manifesting as support resources, things like blog posts based on new findings or lessons learned. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Any help that people can get is going to make them better,\" Phil said.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"from-prototypes-to-production\"\u003eFrom prototypes to production\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne of the more forward-looking parts of the discussion centered on AI-assisted prototyping and vibe coding, where tools like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://lovable.dev/\"\u003eLovable\u003c/a\u003e are making waves. I asked Filip what he makes of this trend and how these tools might impact the Umbraco ecosystem. He acknowledged both the opportunity – and the risk.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We’re seeing some of the horror stories about people not really understanding what a prototype is and what should and shouldn’t go into production,” he observed. “I think as they hear some of those stories, people will start to ask, how do I turn my Lovable prototype into something that I can actually trust?” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI’ve written extensively about this shift in the market and how vibe-coded solutions are replacing software at certain levels. Even \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cursor.com/\"\u003eCursor\u003c/a\u003e – another tool in this ecosystem – recently announced that it would be dumping its headless CMS and using a combination of its own conjured elements to manage its website without a content management system.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOf course, this raises a slew of questions about security, scalability, and governance. Are organizations ready to ensure compliance with vibe-coded solutions? Not likely – and Filip’s betting that these trust factors will continue drawing people to more mature solutions like Umbraco.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“People will be looking at platforms like ours that have user management, data governance, performance, and delivery,” he said. “Then they can ask, how do I turn my prototype into that?” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003ePhil’s broader take on AI’s direction is also a mixture of pragmatism and confidence. As he said, AI moves quickly, but that’s balanced by some of the fundamentals of how LLMs function – things like the underlying methodology and the critical role of context. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“If you stay true to those things, then I think you’re always going to find yourself,” Phil explained. “The people who are going to be able to differentiate themselves are the ones who can collaborate with AI in the best possible way.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"‘phil’-your-cup-–-twice\"\u003e‘Phil’ your cup – twice\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn a market where vendors are racing to declare themselves “AI‑first,” Umbraco is speaking with a clear and unmistakable voice, focusing on a message of AI readiness and open choice. And at a moment when topics like digital sovereignty are permeating every conversation, it’s refreshing to see an open source platform reinforcing its commitments to democratization and transparency while still pushing the AI boundaries.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith MCP as a connective tissue, Umbraco’s two-speed strategy for innovation is providing a sage combo for delivering stability and extensibility. The ace up its sleeve – a dense and loyal open source community – is also giving “The Friendly CMS” a powerful asset for tapping a steady stream of new ideas. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you care about where CMS is heading in an agentic AI world – and where MCP fits in – this conversation with Filip and Phil is going to be worth your time. It's as much about the technical journey as the philosophical one.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBesides, aren't two “Phils” better than one? \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"“the-critic’s-corner”-podcast-with-filip-bech-larsen-and-phil-whittaker\"\u003e“The Critic’s Corner” podcast with Filip Bech-Larsen and Phil SOURCE","id":"1188f5c4-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"open-source","wordpressId":"22","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"d843e9b0-0b73-11f1-b5a7-9d5ff44aeca8","TagId":"1188f5c4-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}},{"name":"Podcast","id":"b94ed070-709a-11f0-98bc-8b848d270cce","slug":"podcast","wordpressId":null,"postTagJoin":{"PostId":"d843e9b0-0b73-11f1-b5a7-9d5ff44aeca8","TagId":"b94ed070-709a-11f0-98bc-8b848d270cce"}},{"name":"The Critic's Corner","id":"b94c8680-709a-11f0-98bc-8b848d270cce","slug":"the-critics-corner","wordpressId":null,"postTagJoin":{"PostId":"d843e9b0-0b73-11f1-b5a7-9d5ff44aeca8","TagId":"b94c8680-709a-11f0-98bc-8b848d270cce"}},{"name":"Umbraco","id":"130b5006-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b","slug":"umbraco","wordpressId":"56","postTagJoin":{"PostId":"d843e9b0-0b73-11f1-b5a7-9d5ff44aeca8","TagId":"130b5006-f421-11ed-9a94-1f002da0f90b"}}],"postProduct":{"id":"5bd3bc20-0b78-11f1-b5a7-9d5ff44aeca8","postId":"d843e9b0-0b73-11f1-b5a7-9d5ff44aeca8","productId":"3b275ce0-f8c3-11ed-843f-05f7aa84865d"},"campaignPost":null,"minutesToRead":13},{"name":"Flying the Agentic Skies: easyJet’s Paul Curtis on Taking Off with Agents and Soaring with MACH","intro":"The CTO of one of Europe’s leading airlines is packing for an agentic future. In our exclusive interview, he gets real about the impacts of AI, the importance of human readiness, and how the MACH Alliance can elevate success in the agent-to-agent ecosystem. ","content":"\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThere’s a moment in the 2009 film \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Up_in_the_Air_(2009_film)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eUp in the Air\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/a\u003e when George Clooney’s character, Ryan Bingham – a lonely corporate gunslinger who spends more time on planes than in his apartment – tells a colleague that life is better with company. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Everybody needs a co-pilot,” he says. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI couldn’t agree more. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBingham has many candid revelations throughout this charming romcom, softening his professional gait as a “hatchet man.” That’s colloquial slang for someone who fires people for a living. Yuck. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOn the upside: During the second act, Bingham surpasses 10 million frequent flyer miles, and the pilot (played by the intrepidly mustached Sam Elliott) delivers the news at 37,000 feet.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"media\"\u003e\u003cdiv data-oembed-url=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fO0Yr1xXtxs\"\u003e\u003cdiv style=\"position:relative;padding-bottom:100%;height:0;padding-bottom:56.2493%\"\u003e\u003ciframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/fO0Yr1xXtxs\" style=\"position:absolute;width:100%;height:100%;top:0;left:0\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; encrypted-media\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDown on the ground, along the evolving runway of \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.ibm.com/think/topics/ai-agents\"\u003eAI agents,\u003c/a\u003e the word “co-pilot” is apropos. Maybe these handy tools can’t plug a sad hole in our hearts, but they’re right by our side, lightening the load and making life better. They've become nearly ubiquitous in our apps, with every tool sporting a prompt-based experience for chatting, searching, or executing tasks.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt's worth noting that an agent isn't a new concept. We've had them bouncing around the stack for years, handing off jobs from one place to another and automating workflows. Even the idea of engaging with a conversational bot was pioneered by \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.newscientist.com/article/2463843-worlds-first-ai-chatbot-has-finally-been-resurrected-after-decades/\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003eMIT's Joseph Weizenbaum,\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:rgb(10,10,10)\"\u003e who built the ELIZA interface back in the late 1960s. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNowadays, you can spot them everywhere in the wild. In the DXP jungle, leading vendors like \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/products/sitecore\"\u003eSitecore\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/products/optimizely\"\u003eOptimizely\u003c/a\u003e have introduced not only omnipresent AI assistants, but also agentic features that work both on-demand and ambiently, with the ability to customize agents for automating an array of duties.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut the potential of agents is evolving – and in quite personal ways, beyond the confines of software ecosystems and into the public atmosphere. Case in point: your mom might not know what an “agent” is, but she’s probably using ChatGPT to plot her parking job at Trader Joe’s. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAgents are becoming more like us. They’re getting human names. Email addresses. Organizational titles. Even \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/video/2026/01/22/william-on-music-in-the-ai-era-and-the-value-of-human-awesomeness.html\"\u003emusic legend Will.I.Am\u003c/a\u003e has become an agentic ambassador, unleashing AI’s creative potential across his music. In a recent interview, he suggested that students might graduate from school with their own agent, trained on their collective knowledge and capable of unlocking their “human awesomeness.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSounds like an exciting future.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut right now, the vision of an agent-to-agent ecosystem – one where agents can move beyond proprietary constraints and connect with websites, applications, and other agents to transact on our behalf – is still trying to get off the ground. According to \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/agentic-panic-new-study-finds-ai-agents-in-production-face-infrastructure-and-reliability-challenges\"\u003eresearch from Cleanlab,\u003c/a\u003e only 5% of enterprises have agentic systems in production, and many are having to refactor key components on a regular basis. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNowhere was the agent maturity race more evident than at last month’s \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://nrfbigshow.nrf.com/\"\u003eNational Retail Federation (NRF) conference\u003c/a\u003e in New York. Commerce has long been the canary in the digital coalmine when it comes to change, and AI was front and center. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFrom accelerating checkout experiences to personalizing shopping, the agent momentum was furious. There’s long been talk of monetizing the answer engines via agentic services, and we’re seeing that come to fruition with \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.americanbanker.com/payments/news/google-shopify-unveil-new-agentic-protocol-for-retailers\"\u003eGoogle’s Universal Commerce Protocol (UCP),\u003c/a\u003e an open standard for agents and systems to work together. With UCP, customers can buy from retailers directly through Google’s AI Mode in the browser, or via the Gemini app. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eGiven this progress, it’s clear that AI is no longer up in the air. It’s a requirement. The problem rests with execution, and most organizations are struggling to taxi down the agentic runway.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image-style-align-center image_resized\" style=\"width:34.86%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1770999589231.png\" alt=\"A person with a beard and mustache\n\nAI-generated content may be incorrect.\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eeasyJet CTO and e-Commerce Director Paul Curtis. Source: LinkedIn\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAt the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/step-into-the-ai-time-machine-jason-cottrell-of-mach-alliance-on-whats-ahead-in-2026\"\u003eMACH Alliance’s\u003c/a\u003e recent \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/the-x-factor-is-ai-mach-alliances-mach-x-and-ai-exchange-hackathon-help-enterprises-face-the-future\"\u003eMACH X Conference\u003c/a\u003e in London, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/paulcurtis/\"\u003ePaul Curtis,\u003c/a\u003e the CTO and e-Commerce director for \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://careers.easyjet.com/en\"\u003eeasyJet\u003c/a\u003e – one of Europe’s largest airline carriers – made a stark prediction about the future of agents, and the real risk that brands face if they don’t get on board.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\"By 2030, we expect 60% of all online transactions to be initiated through agents,” he said. “If you consider how long it takes large enterprises to deliver change, you've got to start \u003ci\u003enow\u003c/i\u003e.\"\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eShort of pressing the passenger call button, Paul is signaling urgent action, ignited by the real-world experience he’s acquiring at easyJet. The company is well into its own AI transformation, buoyed by MACH and composable thinking. But to his point, change is hard – especially for enterprises. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI recently caught up with Paul to discuss how the AI shift is playing out in the travel industry, why mobile is still the essential bridge to the passenger experience, and how agentic systems are forcing us to rethink trust, standards, and the role of change management. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs a member of the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://machalliance.org/ambassadors\"\u003eMACH Alliance Ambassador Program\u003c/a\u003e, Paul also shared how the Alliance’s success formula for AI is deeply rooted in a cultural mindshift, reflecting its prescription for implementing composable patterns and stacks. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt was a first-class conversation that was as much about the journey as the destination.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"a-new-breed-of-‘travel-agent’\"\u003eA new breed of ‘Travel Agent’\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo put the agentic journey in context for this industry, Paul gave me a familiar framework. In his example, he compared AI agents to humans that, once upon a time, understood our personal history and nuances – and used their judgment to facilitate the experience.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Take yourself back to the mid 1990s, when you would walk into a travel agency,” he described. “You might say, ‘I want to go on an adventure holiday, and I want to go in June. What can you offer me?’ They would have a deep understanding of you as a customer. They would know all the potential options that are suitable, based on numerous data points that were relevant in your interaction.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat’s the bar he’s setting for AI with easyJet – a frictionless kind of exchange that leverages context and introduces judgment into the equation. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“What we're trying to do is create a mental model around that,” Paul explained, “to effectively put a bunch of agents together that can fulfill those individual requirements, with the inputs being context about who the customer is, what historical engagements we've had, what are the questions they're asking us, and how do we best service them.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOf course, building AI systems that behave like trusted human specialists – and not opaque black boxes – is a challenging altitude to reach and maintain. This is where Paul is harnessing easyJet’s years of domain expertise to enhance that critical layer of judgment to an agent workforce.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"flight-check:-mobile-first-and-agent-ready\"\u003eFlight check: Mobile-first and agent-ready\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn an omnichannel world, brands need to be everywhere – and on every device. In travel, high-value transactions used to mean one thing: a big screen and a keyboard. Paul noted that for years, serious purchases defaulted to desktops because that’s where the brand experience and consumer confidence lived. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“Historically, there was this notion that every transaction has to be on a desktop above a certain value, because people wanted the confidence of that big screen,” he said. “If I go back four or five years, I would say you're probably looking at around 80% of all transactions being carried out on a desktop when they’re considered high-value transactions.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eToday, that picture has changed dramatically. Airline mobile apps have become digital wallets for every step of the experience – from browsing flights to booking tickets to storing your boarding pass. As Paul said, easyJet has seen a huge shift in usage as the experience has evolved and trust has become foundational. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We’re looking at numbers of about 40% of all transactions through the mobile app,” he shared. “And if we extrapolate the trends, mobile becomes the prevalent channel of engagement within 12 to 18 months.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut as AI answer engines enter the equation, the consumer’s search and discovery behavior is shifting. People are planning trips and researching options using \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://chatgpt.com/\"\u003eChatGPT\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.perplexity.ai/\"\u003ePerplexity\u003c/a\u003e – and while transactions aren’t yet possible, Google’s UCP is \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.axios.com/2026/01/11/google-shopify-ai-shopping-standard-nrf-2026\"\u003ealready lining up with brand partners\u003c/a\u003e like Shopify, Etsy, Walmart, and Target.   \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 style=\"text-align:center\" id=\"“we’re-making-huge-investments-in-our-app,-because-we-do-see-it-as-the-primary-tool-of-engagement,-in-a-way-that’s-reflective-of-what-we-think-the-direction-of-travel-is.”\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cmark class=\"marker-yellow\"\u003e“We’re making huge investments in our app, because we do see it as the primary tool of engagement, in a way that’s reflective of what we think the direction of travel is.”\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eDespite the buzz around answer engines and agents, Paul is clear: the airline app isn’t dead. In fact, investment appears to be accelerating. Hopefully that yields better outcomes, because most airline apps are – in a word – \u003ci\u003eterrible\u003c/i\u003e. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“If you look at other industries, airline apps aren’t a great user experience,” Paul said. “In the last six to 12 months, what’s interesting is that the level of investment being made in airline apps has dramatically increased. British Airways is investing huge amounts of money in theirs, and they clearly see it as a key part of their strategy going forward.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhere mobile really becomes indispensable, Paul argued, is at the physical edge: the airport. The app isn’t just a booking frontend, it’s becoming your identity and travel orchestrator.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image-style-align-center image_resized\" style=\"width:55.56%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/image-1771001618100.png\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eeasyJet mobile app. Source: Google Play Store\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We’re very close to being able to store your passport information securely in your app with biometrics at the airport, so you don't even have to take your passport out of your pocket to travel internationally,” he said. “If we can make your mobile app ubiquitous to every part of the user journey, even through the airport environment, then the value we get from you engaging and transacting with the app versus other channels becomes far more significant.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFrom a CX perspective, there’s a key transformation in play that enriches the value of the mobile channel. Paul sees the industry’s app fabric becoming a kind of modular delivery surface, one that’s mobile-first and agent-ready. And when powered by a composable stack, capabilities can be added incrementally via agent protocols without being locked into current patterns. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eInteracting with all of these environmental touchpoints – physical and digital – is powerful. But executing tasks and transacting takes everything to the next level. Imagine your app telling you it will take an hour and a half to get through airport security. As Paul said, it could automatically provide an alternative route or even upsell a fast track that saves you time.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eHaving this flexible mobile strategy sounds like the runway to the next wave of agent-powered services. But with AI, change is the status quo. As the answer engines evolve to encompass transactions, they’re likely to become a more prolific channel in the passenger journey. This is where \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.conductor.com/academy/answer-engine-optimization/\"\u003eAEO (Answer Engine Optimization)\u003c/a\u003e is becoming a more pronounced part of the digital strategy.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“We’re making huge investments in our app, because we do see it as the primary tool of engagement,” Paul said, “in a way that’s reflective of what we think the direction of travel is.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"turbulence:-security,-compromised-agents,-and-observability\"\u003eTurbulence: Security, compromised agents, and observability\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003ePaul was blunt about the security challenges facing agentic systems. It’s something I also discussed with \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/agentic-panic-new-study-finds-ai-agents-in-production-face-infrastructure-and-reliability-challenges\"\u003eCurtis Northcutt of Cleanlab\u003c/a\u003e late last year. AI agents in production face a multitude of unseen problems, from infrastructure instability to poor performance. Paul is particularly worried about malicious agents quietly embedded in chains.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“The elephant in the room that we're not really talking about is how do we ensure the adoption of these agent ecosystems, but in a secure way?” he said. “I think we’re on the cusp of a bit of an explosion of agents being compromised. If you look at the threat of being able to inject a corrupt agent into a chain of agents that can just sit there silently, collecting data somewhere else. I mean, it's terrifying.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhat makes it worse is how casually users and enterprises are already trusting these systems. As I said in my keynote at the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/beyond-the-gate-cms-kickoff-26-explored-the-ai-frontier-while-focusing-on-fundamentals\"\u003eBoye \u0026amp; Company CMS Kickoff\u003c/a\u003e last month, we often hook things up without considering the consequences – something that created problems in the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.akamai.com/glossary/what-are-api-security-breaches\"\u003eearly days of APIs\u003c/a\u003e with weak authentication, excessive data exposure, and shadow endpoints.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“What's been fascinating for me is the level of trust that consumers have had in a lot of these agentic solutions in terms of the data they're willing to share,” he explained. “The agentic browsers they're willing to install on their desktops that can have access to all of their local credentials. I mean, it's astonishing.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSo what can we do about it? This is an area where the MACH Alliance can bring calm to the storm through greater awareness, training, and education – something they’ve done consistently through the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/mach-alliance-taps-dylan-valade-of-abbott-to-drive-expanding-ridemach-education-program\"\u003erideMACH program.\u003c/a\u003e As Paul said, having the right industry expertise and partnerships is key, as this is still a nascent field. Certification could be an opportunity to shore up skills for individuals and organizations and provide more validation.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eObservability is also a critical requirement. Most software tools with agents don’t offer line-of-sight into agent performance and uptime (think container health dashboards in \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.datadoghq.com/\"\u003eDatadog\u003c/a\u003e). This is something that \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.rubrik.com/insights/ai-observability\"\u003eplatforms like Rubrik\u003c/a\u003e are pioneering, but we can expect more native tooling to emerge. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhile the turbulence is real, awareness around these issues is elevating across IT organizations. Achieving a credible operational model for agentic systems will be a key objective, and an area where enterprises will require tangible resilience.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"piloting-an-agentic-ai-journey-with-a-mach-mindset-\"\u003ePiloting an agentic AI journey with a MACH mindset \u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eAt \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/the-deep-dish-on-composable-6-tasty-takeaways-from-the-mach-alliances-2025-conference\"\u003e“The Composable Conference”\u003c/a\u003e in Chicago last year, Paul and I had an intersection with CMS strategist and analyst \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/mdemeny/\"\u003eMark Demeny.\u003c/a\u003e We all noted the vibe around agentic commerce and the focus on \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://modelcontextprotocol.io/docs/getting-started/intro\"\u003eMCP (Model Context Protocol),\u003c/a\u003e but also the elevated drumbeat surrounding the MACH Alliance’s focus on AI.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis isn’t new. I’ve been covering the rise of AI across the Alliance’s messaging for the last few years, reflecting trends across the industry. As \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/chadsolomonson/\"\u003eChad Solomonson of digital agency RDA\u003c/a\u003e said during a recent presentation, composability has won the battle – and in many ways, it’s offering a flexible flight plan for scaling and experimenting with AI.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe data appears to codify this. According to the \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cts.businesswire.com/ct/CT?id=smartlink\u0026amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fmachalliance.org%2Fglobal-annual-research\u0026amp;esheet=54242130\u0026amp;newsitemid=20250423626378\u0026amp;lan=en-US\u0026amp;anchor=2025+MACH+Alliance+Global+Annual+Research\u0026amp;index=4\u0026amp;md5=8b35e7c9765b71263fa3b549fb481c06\"\u003eMACH Alliance Global Annual Research\u003c/a\u003e report, 77% of organizations well into their composable journey are dramatically ahead in their AI adoption. That’s compared to only 36% of those new to MACH. The research suggests that MACH's flexible, connected, and open foundation can translate into faster, more successful AI outcomes that give enterprises an edge in the agentic arms race. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cfigure class=\"image image-style-align-center image_resized\" style=\"width:85.61%\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/02/mach-alliance-agent-ecosystems-website.png\" /\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"text-small\" style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003e\u003ci\u003eThe MACH Alliance Agent Ecosystem website.\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn August of 2025, the Alliance made a notable pivot, mapping its vision to unlock trusted, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/an-alliance-for-ai-to-unlock-trusted-agent-to-agent-ecosystems-the-mach-alliance-is-evolving\"\u003eagent-to-agent ecosystems.\u003c/a\u003e The organization launched a dedicated website with the stated goal of evolving enterprise AI architectures with a new \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/mach-alliance-aims-to-evolve-enterprise-ai-architecture-with-new-end-user-leadership-model\"\u003eend-user leadership model.\u003c/a\u003e From the top down, the advocacy group would now mine more guidance from experienced industry practitioners. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis included the appointment of \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/jasoncottrell/\"\u003eJason Cottrell, CEO of digital agency Orium,\u003c/a\u003e as the Alliance’s new president. \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/step-into-the-ai-time-machine-jason-cottrell-of-mach-alliance-on-whats-ahead-in-2026\"\u003eI spoke to Jason\u003c/a\u003e in December about these recent shifts and what he sees ahead for MACH and AI. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf I’ve monitored one glaring gap in this agentic hype, it’s that the Alliance has experienced a bit of an identity crisis. That said, finding your footing in the AI game is a bit like walking a tightrope with an elephant on your back. As an Alliance ambassador, I asked Paul where he sees the value evolving, and he drew a straight line from MACH principles to agent ecosystems.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“This is one of the more fascinating debates that we're having at the moment, particularly at a board level within MACH,” he said. “I think the evolution of agentic plays very well to the strengths of what MACH brings to the table. If you look at the core principles that should be in place to support having a really good agentic ecosystem – principles around composability, interoperability, standard data models – these are all things that are highly relevant to that agent ecosystem.” \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt’s a solid point. And last year, the MACH Alliance delivered more actionable resources to maintain these standards, including its \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/a-new-game-for-interoperability-heres-why-the-mach-alliances-open-data-model-is-a-winner\"\u003eOpen Data Model\u003c/a\u003e. But AI is changing rapidly, and I asked Paul how standardized things should get around agent requirements.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“I think the challenge for us is getting the right balance between defining a core set of principles and standards and being really prescriptive about how those agents are constructed,” he replied. “Do we want to lean more towards the Agile manifesto approach, where it's kind of a tablet of principles? Or prescriptive data models that should be adopted if you're creating a basket agent or whatever it happens to be?”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese are great questions, and we’re still too early to fully answer them. In the meantime, enterprise software vendors are building their own proprietary agent systems that offer both opportunities and dependencies. If true agent-to-agent ecosystems are going to thrive, a standards-driven body like MACH Alliance may be one of the few credible venues to define open agent patterns that avoid vendor lock-in.\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"piloting-the-agentic-course-with-‘human-readiness’\"\u003ePiloting the agentic course with ‘human readiness’\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn my recent keynote at CMS Kickoff 26, I mentioned how the phrase “human in the loop” is beginning to feel like a marketing platitude. I’m not disparaging platforms, nor am I suggesting that their tooling doesn’t position humans in some kind of “loop.” But it’s just scratching the surface. Like AI, it needs context – and we need to define just how valuable our human judgment is to an AI-enabled process or workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen I talked to Paul, it was clear just how important this judgment really is. As we discussed, adopting the right tools to enhance human work is key, but adoption is often a source of friction – which can be painful but essential. According to MIT, avoiding this friction is why \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/jasonsnyder/2025/08/26/mit-finds-95-of-genai-pilots-fail-because-companies-avoid-friction/\"\u003e95% of GenAI projects fail\u003c/a\u003e before they reach production.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBut there’s also friction on the people side. Real barriers exist with things like human dynamics, change management, and cultural adaptation. Too often, organizations deploying AI don’t lead with transparency, leaving gaps in knowledge and skill training. In fact, according to PwC, \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.pwc.com/ca/en/media/release/pwc-canada-iso-42001-ai-trust-certification.html\"\u003e45% of Canadian CEOs\u003c/a\u003e said they haven’t even formalized responsible AI and risk processes. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003ch4 style=\"text-align:center\" id=\"-\"\u003e \u003c/h4\u003e\u003ch4 style=\"text-align:center\" id=\"“ai-takes-mechanical-parts-of-your-job-away-so-you-can-do-more-of-the-human-ones.-it's-not-going-to-replace-our-human-judgment-or-our-creativity.”\"\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cmark class=\"marker-yellow\"\u003e“AI takes mechanical parts of your job away so you can do more of the human ones. It's not going to replace our human judgment or our creativity.”\u003c/mark\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp style=\"text-align:center\"\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn many cases, the greatest challenge isn't choosing platforms or models, it's navigating the complex human landscape of transformation. To help support the human part of the equation, the MACH Alliance has developed programs like its \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/mach-alliance-launches-new-mach-ai-exchange-to-help-enterprises-streamline-ai-adoption\"\u003eMACH AI Exchange\u003c/a\u003e, a hands-on program administered by industry professionals to provide a stronger foundation for streamlining AI adoption.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn lockstep, Paul adamantly agreed that adoption issues surrounding AI are more human than technical – at least at this stage. Most enterprises have over-rotated on infrastructure and under-invested in what he calls “human readiness.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“There's been this real focus on what I would call ‘technical readiness’ to adopt AI,” he said. “The bit we've really missed is actually the ‘human readiness.’ How do we actually adopt AI in an effective way?”\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eI’ve written extensively about the critical role of change management in organizations, particularly in this hyperbolic period of AI transformation. As Paul said, the critical foundation of human readiness will be key to making the journey successful.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor enterprises, enrolling people in the vision of a hybrid AI/human workforce is key. As Paul reinforced, it’s not just about declaring how AI will drive efficiency and unlock productivity. Those are vague promises. He’s advocating for a different narrative.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e“AI takes mechanical parts of your job away so you can do more of the human ones,” he said. “It's not going to replace our human judgment or our creativity.”\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"is-the-future-up-in-the-air?\"\u003eIs the future up in the air?\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003eA lot of it is. That much was evident in the predictions from industry luminaries who mused about 2026 and what lies ahead. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne person who continues to get it right (in my humble opinion) is \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://biilmann.blog/articles/predictions-for-2026/\"\u003eNetlify’s Matt Biilmann,\u003c/a\u003e who first wrote about the rise of \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/its-an-ai-agent-world-is-agent-experience-the-secret-weapon-for-controlling-the-chaos\"\u003e“Agent Experience”\u003c/a\u003e – known in some parts of Silicon Valley simply as “AX” – back in early 2025. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs Matt recently told me, foundational model providers are enabling companies to apply truly autonomous agents to bigger parts of the work they’re doing, and the landscape is expanding. AX is becoming a key concern not just for dev tools, but for any kind of digital experience. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd as vibe coding becomes the norm (see \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/vibe-coding-fomo-fimoai-offers-easy-website-building-with-ai-native-cms-capabilities\"\u003eFIMO’s latest site builder,\u003c/a\u003e or \u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://cmscritic.com/from-ai-idea-to-production-ready-app-in-minutes-meet-domos-new-app-catalyst\"\u003eDOMO’s latest app builder\u003c/a\u003e) and Google’s UCP takes hold, we’re going to see seismic shifts across our tools and businesses. \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn all of this, there are risks. Security tops the list. We need more – and better – observability. Ultimately, agent standards could become an essential foundation of an open agent-to-agent ecosystem, but not at the cost of stymying innovation. This is where the MACH Alliance could provide independent guardrails and resources for shaping an agent marketplace that is modular, interoperable, and capable of extending into new frontiers.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eMost importantly, we need smart people who can bring judgment and context to help orchestrate all of this. As Paul said, it’s the “human readiness” that we’re lacking, and AI requires a change management strategy that puts people in the pilot's seat.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSo buckle up. This is how we fly the agentic skies.\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003chr /\u003e\u003ch3 id=\"upcoming-events\"\u003eUpcoming Events\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cp\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cimg style=\"width:34.15%\" src=\"https://cmscritic.com/ms-content/uploads/2026/01/logo_jday_hor.png\" /\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003ch4 id=\"joomladay-usa-2026\"\u003e\u003ca target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"https://www.jdayusa.com/\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"color:hsl(210,75%,60%)\"\u003eJoomlaDay USA 2026\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eApril 29 - May 2, 2026 – Delray Beach, Florida\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBe part of the Joomla community in one of the most iconic cities in the world!
